***wind.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> wind (1221)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">winde</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">wind</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">wind</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">wind</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*windaz</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*h₂wéh₁n̥tos</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">wind</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from earlier <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*h₂wéh₁n̥ts</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">wind</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, derived from the present participle of <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*h₂weh₁-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to blow</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">wind</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Wind</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Frisian_language" class="extiw" title="w:West Frisian language">West Frisian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fy">wyn</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norwegian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Norwegian language">Norwegian</a></span> and <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swedish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Swedish language">Swedish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sv">vind</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Icelandic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Icelandic language">Icelandic</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="is">vindur</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">ventus</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Welsh_language" class="extiw" title="w:Welsh language">Welsh</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="cy">gwynt</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit" class="extiw" title="w:Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a></span> <i class="Deva mention" lang="sa">वात</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="sa-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">vā́ta</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Russian language">Russian</a></span> <i class="Cyrl mention" lang="ru"><a href = vnd.unilang:ветер.html>ве́тер</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="ru-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">véter</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren lang="sq">bundë</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">strong damp wind</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<div class="sister-wikipedia sister-project noprint floatright" style="border: 1px solid aaa; font-size: 90%; background: f9f9f9; width: 250px; padding: 4px; text-align: left;"><div style="float: left;"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/44px-Wikipedia-logo.png" decoding="async" width="44" height="44" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/66px-Wikipedia-logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/88px-Wikipedia-logo.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="200" /></div></div><div style="margin-left: 60px;">English Wikipedia has an article on:<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beaufort_scale" class="extiw" title="w:Beaufort scale">Beaufort scale</a></b></div></div><span class="interProject"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beaufort_scale" class="extiw" title="w:Beaufort scale">Wikipedia </a></span></div>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">wind</strong> (<i>countable and uncountable</i>, <i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">winds</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">countable<span class="ib-comma">,</span> uncountable</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Real or perceived movement of atmospheric air usually caused by convection or differences in air pressure.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The <b>wind</b> blew through her hair as she stood on the deck of the ship.</i></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">As they accelerated onto the motorway, the <b>wind</b> tore the plywood off the car's roof-rack.</i></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The <b>winds</b> in Chicago are fierce.</i></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">There was a sudden <span class="Latn" lang="en">gust</span> of <b>wind</b><i>.</i></i></div></dd></dl>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2013</b> June 29,  “<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.economist.com/news/asia/21580154-forest-fires-bring-record-levels-air-pollution-and-end-not-sight-unspontaneous">Unspontaneous combustion</a>”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Economist" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Economist">The Economist</a></cite>, volume 407, number 8842, page 29:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Since the mid-1980s, when Indonesia first began to clear its bountiful forests on an industrial scale in favour of lucrative palm-oil plantations, “haze” has become an almost annual occurrence in South-East Asia. The cheapest way to clear logged woodland is to burn it, producing an acrid cloud of foul white smoke that, carried by the <b>wind</b>, can cover hundreds, or even thousands, of square miles.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>Air artificially put in motion by any force or action.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">the <b>wind</b> of a cannon ball;  the <b>wind</b> of a bellows</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">countable<span class="ib-comma">,</span> uncountable</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The ability to breathe easily.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">After the second lap he was already out of <b>wind</b>.</i></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The fall knocked the <b>wind</b> out of him.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>News of an event, especially by hearsay or gossip. <span class="use-with-mention">(Used with catch, often in the past tense.)</span>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">Steve caught <b>wind</b> of Martha's dalliance with his best friend.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>One of the five basic elements in Indian and Japanese models of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_element" class="extiw" title="w:Classical element">Classical elements</a>).</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">uncountable<span class="ib-comma">,</span> colloquial</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Flatus.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">Eww. Someone just passed <b>wind</b>.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>Breath modulated by the respiratory and vocal organs, or by an instrument.
<ul><li><span class="maintenance-line" style="color: 777777;">(Can we date this quote by John Dryden and provide title, author's full name, and other details?)</span>
<dl><dd>Their instruments were various in their kind, / Some for the bow, and some for breathing <b>wind</b>.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">music</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The woodwind section of an orchestra.  Occasionally also used to include the brass section.</li>
<li>A direction from which the wind may blow; a point of the compass; especially, one of the cardinal points, which are often called the "four winds".
<ul><li>Bible, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ezekiel" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Ezekiel">Ezekiel</a> xxxvii. 9
<dl><dd>Come from the four <b>winds</b>, O breath, and breathe upon these slain.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1898</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill_(novelist)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Winston Churchill (novelist)">Winston Churchill</a>,  chapter 5, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Celebrity" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Celebrity">The Celebrity</a></cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">When this conversation was repeated in detail within the hearing of the young woman in question, and undoubtedly for his benefit, Mr. Trevor threw shame to the <b>winds</b> and scandalized the Misses Brewster then and there by proclaiming his father to have been a country storekeeper.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>Types of playing-tile in the game of mah-jongg, named after the four winds.</li>
<li>A disease of sheep, in which the intestines are distended with air, or rather affected with a violent inflammation. It occurs immediately after shearing.</li>
<li>Mere breath or talk; empty effort; idle words.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1667</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Milton" class="extiw" title="w:John Milton">John Milton</a>,  “Book 6”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paradise_Lost" class="extiw" title="w:Paradise Lost">Paradise Lost. A Poem Written in Ten Books</a></cite>, London |  Printed [by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_Simmons" class="extiw" title="w:Samuel Simmons">Samuel Simmons</a>], and are to be sold by Peter Parker<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="under Creed Church neer Aldgate;">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span> [a]nd by Robert Boulter<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="at the Turks Head in Bishopsgate-street;">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span> [a]nd Matthias Walker,<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="under St. Dunstons Church in Fleet-street">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/228722708">228722708</a></small> |  republished as  <cite>Paradise Lost in Ten Books: The Text Exactly Reproduced from the First Edition of 1667:<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="With an Appendix Containing the Additions Made in Later Issues and a Monograph on the Original Publication of the Poem">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></cite>, London |  Basil Montagu Pickering<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="196 Piccadilly">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, 1873, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/230729554">230729554</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Nor think thou with <b>wind</b> / Of airy threats to awe.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1946</b>,  George Orwell,  <cite>Politics and the English Language</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Political language is designed to make lies sound truthful and murder respectable, and to give an appearance of solidity to pure <b>wind</b>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>A bird, the dotterel.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">boxing<span class="ib-comma">,</span> slang</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The region of the solar plexus, where a blow may paralyze the diaphragm and cause temporary loss of breath or other injury.</li></ol>

<ul><li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">movement of air</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span><span class="ib-colon sense-qualifier-colon">:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en">breeze</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">draft</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">gale</span>; see also Thesaurus:wind</li>

<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">wind</strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">winds</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">winding</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">winded</b> <i>or</i> <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">proscribed</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">wound</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To blow air through a wind instrument or horn to make a sound.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1913</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constance_Holme" class="extiw" title="w:Constance Holme">Edith Constance Holme</a>,  <cite>Crump Folk Going Home</cite>, page 136:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Something higher must lie at the back of that eager response to pack-music and <b>winded</b> horn — something born of the smell of the good earth</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To cause (someone) to become breathless, as by a blow to the abdomen, or by physical exertion, running, etc.
<dl><dd><i>The boxer was <b>winded</b> during round two.</i></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To cause a baby to bring up wind by patting its back after being fed.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To turn a boat or ship around, so that the wind strikes it on the opposite side.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To expose to the <a class="mw-selflink selflink">wind</a>; to winnow; to ventilate.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To perceive or follow by scent.
<dl><dd><i>The hounds <b>winded</b> the game.</i></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To rest (a horse, etc.) in order to allow the breath to be recovered; to breathe.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To turn a windmill so that its sails face into the wind.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-1"> | 1 | </a></sup></li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li>The form “wound” in the past is occasionally found in reference to blowing a horn, but is often considered to be erroneous. The October 1875 issue of <i>The Galaxy</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=NS8ZAAAAYAAJamp;pg=PA556">disparaged this usage</a> as a “very ridiculous mistake” arising from a misunderstanding of the word's meaning.</li>
<li>A similar solecism occurs in the use (in this sense) of the pronunciation <span class="IPA">/waɪnd/</span>, sometimes heard in singing and oral reading of verse  e.g. The huntsman <span class="IPA">/waɪndz/</span> his horn.</li></ul>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">winden</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">windan</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*windaną</i>. Compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Frisian_language" class="extiw" title="w:West Frisian language">West Frisian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fy">wine</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low_German" class="extiw" title="w:Low German">Low German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nds">winden</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">winden</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">winden</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Danish language">Danish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="da">vinde</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walloon_language" class="extiw" title="w:Walloon language">Walloon</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="wa">windea</i>. See also the related term <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">wend</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb_2">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">wind</strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">winds</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">winding</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">wound</b> <i>or</i> <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">archaic</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">winded</b>)
</p>
<ol><li class="senseid" id="English-turn_coils"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To turn coils of (a cord or something similar) around something.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">to <b>wind</b> thread on a spool or into a ball</i></div></dd></dl>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1667</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Milton" class="extiw" title="w:John Milton">John Milton</a>,  “Book 9”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paradise_Lost" class="extiw" title="w:Paradise Lost">Paradise Lost. Peter Parker<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="under Creed Church neer Aldgate;">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span> [a]nd by Robert Boulter<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="at the Turks Head in Bishopsgate-street;">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span> [a]nd Matthias Walker,<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="under St. Dunstons Church in Fleet-street">…</span><span Original Publication of the Poem">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></cite>, London |  Basil Montagu Pickering<span arbour.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1906</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanley_J._Weyman" class="extiw" title="w:Stanley J. Weyman">Stanley J[ohn] Weyman</a>,  chapter I, in  <cite>Chippinge Borough</cite>, New York, N.Y. |  McClure, Phillips amp; Co., <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/580270828">580270828</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/chippingeborough00weymuoftpage/01/mode/1up/">page 01</a>:</span><dl><dd></dd></dl></div>
<dl><dd>It was April 22, 1831, and a young man was walking down Whitehall in the direction of Parliament Street. He wore shepherd's plaid trousers and the swallow-tail coat of the day, with a figured muslin cravat <b>wound</b> about his wide-spread collar.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To tighten the spring of a clockwork mechanism such as that of a clock.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">Please <b>wind</b> that old-fashioned alarm clock.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To entwist; to enfold; to encircle.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><i><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr></i> <b>1595–1596</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Shakespeare" class="extiw" title="w:William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>,  “<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_Midsummer_Night%27s_Dream" class="extiw" title="w:A Midsummer Night | s Dream">A Midsommer Nights Dreame</a>”, in  <cite>Mr. William Shakespeares Comedies, Histories, amp; Tragedies: Published According to the True Originall Copies</cite> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Folio" class="extiw" title="w:First Folio">First Folio</a>), London |  Printed by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Jaggard" class="extiw" title="w:William Jaggard">Isaac Iaggard</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Blount" class="extiw" title="w:Edward Blount">Ed[ward] Blount</a>, published 1623, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/606515358">606515358</a></small>,  | Act IV, scene i | :</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Sleep, and I will <b>wind</b> thee in arms.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To travel in a way that is not straight.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">Vines <b>wind</b> round a pole. |  The river <b>winds</b> through the plain.</i></div></dd></dl>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1829</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_Scott" class="extiw" title="w:Walter Scott">Walter Scott</a>,  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anne_of_Geierstein" class="extiw" title="w:Anne of Geierstein">Anne of Geierstein</a></cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">He therefore turned him to the steep and rocky path which<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span><b>winded</b> through the thickets of wild boxwood and other low aromatic shrubs.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>1751</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Gray" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Thomas Gray">Thomas Gray</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:">Elegy Written in a Country Churchyard</a>
<dl><dd>The lowing herd <b>wind</b> slowly o'er the lea.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1898</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill_(novelist)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Winston Churchill (novelist)">Winston Churchill</a>,  chapter 4, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Celebrity" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Celebrity">The Celebrity</a></cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Judge Short had gone to town, and Farrar was off for a three days' cruise up the lake. I was bitterly regretting I had not gone with him when the distant notes of a coach horn reached my ear, and I descried a four-in-hand <b>winding</b> its way up the inn road from the direction of Mohair.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>1969</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_McCartney" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Long_and_Winding_Road" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Long and Winding Road">The Long and Winding Road</a></i>
<dl><dd>The long and <b>winding</b> road / That leads to your door / Will never disappear.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To have complete control over; to turn and bend at one's pleasure; to vary or alter or will; to regulate; to govern.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1591</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Shakespeare" class="extiw" title="w:William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>,  “<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_VI,_Part_1" class="extiw" title="w:Henry VI, Part 1">The First Part of Henry the Sixt</a>”, in  <cite>Mr. William Shakespeares Comedies, Histories, amp; Tragedies: Published According to the True Originall Copies</cite> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Folio" class="extiw" title="w:First Folio">First Folio</a>), London |  Printed by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Jaggard" class="extiw" title="w:William Jaggard">Isaac Iaggard</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Blount" class="extiw" title="w:Edward Blount">Ed[ward] Blount</a>, published 1623, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/606515358">606515358</a></small>, [Act IV, scene i]:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">to turn and <b>wind</b> a fiery Pegasus</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><span class="maintenance-line" style="color: 777777;">(Can we date this quote by Robert Herrick (poet) and provide title, author's full name, and other details?)</span>
<dl><dd>Gifts blind the wise, and bribes do please / And <b>wind</b> all other witnesses.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>12 October 1710</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Addison" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Joseph Addison">Joseph Addison</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Examiner_(1710%E2%80%931714)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Examiner (1710–1714)">The Examiner</a> No. 5</i>
<dl><dd>Were our legislature vested in the person of our prince, he might doubtless <b>wind</b> and turn our constitution at his pleasure.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To introduce by insinuation; to insinuate.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><i><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr></i> <b>1608–1609</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Shakespeare" class="extiw" title="w:William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>,  “<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coriolanus" class="extiw" title="w:Coriolanus">The Tragedy of Coriolanus</a>”, in  <cite>Mr. William Shakespeares Comedies, Histories, amp; Tragedies: Published According to the True Originall Copies</cite> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Folio" class="extiw" title="w:First Folio">First Folio</a>), London |  Printed by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Jaggard" class="extiw" title="w:William Jaggard">Isaac Iaggard</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Blount" class="extiw" title="w:Edward Blount">Ed[ward] Blount</a>, published 1623, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/606515358">606515358</a></small>, [Act III, scene iii]:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">You have contrived<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span>to <b>wind</b> / Yourself into a power tyrannical.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><span class="maintenance-line" style="color: 777777;">(Can we date this quote by Government of Tongues and provide title, author's full name, and other details?)</span>
<dl><dd>little arts and dexterities they have to <b>wind</b> in such things into discourse</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To cover or surround with something coiled about.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">to <b>wind</b> a rope with twine</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To cause to move by exerting a winding force; to haul or hoist, as by a winch.
<ul><li><b>2012</b>, "Rural Affairs", Anna Hutton-North, Lulu.com →ISBN <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.no/books?id=m7bZAwAAQBAJamp;pg=PA33amp;lpg=PA33amp;dq=%22wound+the+window%22amp;source=blamp;ots=snv5JI1qoQamp;sig=yTknoCP9aVabexTmUJfCmPpJ7Xwamp;hl=noamp;sa=Xamp;ved=0ahUKEwihoMH-uPvYAhWJesAKHUIYAJkQ6AEIODAEv=onepageamp;q=%22wound%20the%20window%22amp;f=false">[1]</a>
<dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Quickly she slammed the door shut and panicking <b>wound</b> the window up as fast as her slippery fingers would allow.</span></div></dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> nautical</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To turn (a ship) around, end for end.</li></ol>

<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">wind</strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">winds</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>The act of winding or turning; a turn; a bend; a twist.</li></ol>

<p><b>wing</b>

***wit.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> wit (6394)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">wit</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">witt</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">understanding, intellect, sense, knowledge, consciousness, conscience</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*witją</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">knowledge, reason</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*weyd-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">see, know</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">weet</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Witz</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Danish language">Danish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="da">vid</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swedish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Swedish language">Swedish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sv">vett</i>, 
<span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bokm%C3%A5l" class="extiw" title="w:Bokmål">Norwegian Bokmål</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nb">vett</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gothic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Gothic language">Gothic</a></span> <i class="Goth mention" lang="got">𐌿𐌽𐍅𐌹𐍄𐌹</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="got-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">unwiti</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">ignorance</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">videō</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">see</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Russian language">Russian</a></span> <i class="Cyrl mention" lang="ru"><a href = vnd.unilang:видеть.html>ви́деть</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="ru-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">vídetʹ</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Compare <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">wise</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">wit</strong> (<i>countable and uncountable</i>, <i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">wits</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">now  usually  in the plural<span class="ib-comma">,</span> plural only</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Sanity.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">He's gone completely out of his <b>wits</b>.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete  usually  in the plural</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The senses.</li>
<li>Intellectual ability; faculty of thinking, reasoning.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">Where she has gone to is beyond the <b>wit</b> of man to say.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>The ability to think quickly; mental cleverness, especially under short time constraints.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">My father had a quick <b>wit</b> and a steady hand.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>Intelligence; common sense.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The opportunity was right in front of you, and you didn't even have the <b>wit</b> to take it!</i></div></dd></dl>
<ul><li><b>1460-1500</b>, <i>The Towneley Plays</i>ː
<dl><dd>I give the <b>wit</b>, I give the strength, of all thou seest, of breadth and length; thou shalt be wonder-wise, mirth and joy to have at will, all thy liking to fulfill, and dwell in paradise.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1609</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Shakespeare" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sonnet_23" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Sonnet 23">Sonnet 23</a><sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.opensourceshakespeare.org/views/sonnets/sonnet_view.php?Sonnet=23">[1]</a></sup>:</i>
<dl><dd>O, learn to read what silent love hath writ:</dd>
<dd>To hear with eyes belongs to love's fine <b>wit</b>.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>Humour, especially when clever or quick.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The best man's speech was hilarious, full of <b>wit</b> and charm.</i></div></dd></dl>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1898</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill_(novelist)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Winston Churchill (novelist)">Winston Churchill</a>,  chapter 8, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Celebrity" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Celebrity">The Celebrity</a></cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The humor of my proposition appealed more strongly to Miss Trevor than I had looked for, and from that time forward she became her old self again;<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span>. Our table in the dining-room became again the abode of scintillating <b>wit</b> and caustic repartee, Farrar bracing up to his old standard, and the demand for seats in the vicinity rose to an animated competition.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1996</b> February 4,  “<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scenes_from_the_Class_Struggle_in_Springfield" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Scenes from the Class Struggle in Springfield">Scenes from the Class Struggle in Springfield</a>”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Simpsons" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></cite>, season 7, episode 14, written by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jennifer_Crittenden" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Jennifer Crittenden">Jennifer Crittenden</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><i>Evelyn Peters:</i> "Don't worry, Marge. Her idea of <b>wit</b> is nothing more than an incisive observation humorously phrased and delivered with impeccable timing".</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>1991</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Fry" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Stephen Fry">Stephen Fry</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Liar_(novel)" class="extiw" title="w:The Liar (novel)">The Liar</a></i>, p. 37:
<dl><dd>...the cemetery—which people of shattering <b>wit</b> like Sampson never tired of calling ‘the dead centre of town’...</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>A person who tells funny anecdotes or jokes; someone witty.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">Your friend is quite a <b>wit</b>, isn't he?</i></div></dd></dl>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1601</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Jonson" class="extiw" title="w:Ben Jonson">Ben Jonson</a>,  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poetaster_(play)" class="extiw" title="w:Poetaster (play)">Poetaster or The Arraignment:<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="As it hath beene Sundry Times Priuately Acted in the Blacke Friers, by the Children of Her Maiesties Chappell">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></a></cite>, London |  Printed [by R. Bradock] for M[atthew] L[ownes]<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="and are to be sould in Saint Dunstans Church-yarde">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, published 1602, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/316392309">316392309</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/poetasterorarrai00jons_0page/n62/mode/1up">Act III, scene iv</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><i>Tuc</i>[<i>ca</i>]. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> Can thy Author doe it impudently enough? / <i>Hiſt</i>[<i>rio</i>]. O, I warrant you, Captaine: and ſpitefully inough too; he ha's one of the moſt ouerflowing villanous <b>wits</b>, in <i>Rome</i>. He will ſlander any man that breathes; If he diſguſt him. / <i>Tucca</i>. I'le know the poor, egregious, nitty Raſcall; and he haue ſuch commendable Qualities, I'le cheriſh him: <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>

<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">witen</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">witan</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*witaną</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*weyd-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">see, know</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Icelandic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Icelandic language">Icelandic</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="is">vita</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">weten</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">wissen</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swedish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Swedish language">Swedish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sv">veta</i>, and <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">videō</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">I see</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Compare <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">guide</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">wit</strong> <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">see <a href="Conjugation">below</a> for this verb’s conjugation</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span>
</p>
<ol><li class="senseid" id="English-know"> <span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive, intransitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> chiefly archaic</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Know, be aware of <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">constructed with <b>of</b> when used intransitively</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span>.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">You committed terrible actions — to <b>wit</b>, murder and theft — and should be punished accordingly.</i></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">They are meddling in matters that men should not <b>wit</b> of.</i></div></dd></dl>
<ul><li><b>1611</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_James_Version" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:King James Version">King James Version</a>, Exodus 2:3–4:
<dl><dd>And when she could not longer hide him, she took for him an ark of bulrushes, and daubed it with slime and with pitch, and put the child therein; and she laid it in the flags by the river's brink. And his sister stood afar off, to <b>wit</b> what would be done to him.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1849</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dante_Gabriel_Rossetti" class="extiw" title="w:Dante Gabriel Rossetti">Dante Gabriel Rossetti</a>, <i>St. Luke the Painter</i>, lines 5–8
<dl><dd>but soon having <b>wist</b></dd>
<dd>How sky-breadth and field-silence and this day</dd>
<dd>Are symbols also in some deeper way,</dd>
<dd>She looked through these to God and was God’s priest.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li>As a preterite-present verb, the third-person singular indicative form is not <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">wits</i> but <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">wot</i>; the plural indicative forms conform to the infinitive: <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">we wit</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">ye wit</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">they wit</i>.</li>
<li><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">To wit</i> is now defective because it can only be used in the infinitive.</li></ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Derived_terms_2">Derived terms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">bewit</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">to wit</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">unwitting</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">witness</span></li></ul>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_3">Etymology 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">with</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Preposition">Preposition</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> wolf (4475)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">wolf</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">wulf</i>, <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">ƿulf</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-West_Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-West Germanic language">Proto-West Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gmw-pro">*wulf</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*wulfaz</i> (compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saterland_Frisian" class="extiw" title="w:Saterland Frisian">Saterland Frisian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="stq">Wulf</i>, West Frisian and <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">wolf</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Wolf</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norwegian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Norwegian language">Norwegian</a></span> and <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Danish language">Danish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="da">ulv</i>), from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*wĺ̥kʷos</i> (compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit" class="extiw" title="w:Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a></span> <i class="Deva mention" lang="sa">वृक</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="sa-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">vṛ́ka</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Persian language">Persian</a></span> <i class="fa-Arab mention" lang="fa">گرگ</i> |  <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="fa-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">gorg</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuanian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="lt">vilkas</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Russian language">Russian</a></span> <i class="Cyrl mention" lang="ru"><a href = vnd.unilang:волк.html>волк</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="ru-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">volk</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albanian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Albanian language">Albanian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sq">ujk</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">lupus</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_language" class="extiw" title="w:Greek language">Greek</a></span> <i class="Grek mention" lang="el">λύκος</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="el-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">lýkos</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tocharian_languages" class="extiw" title="w:Tocharian languages">Tocharian B</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="txb">walkwe</i>).
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">wolf</strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">wolves</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>The gray wolf, specifically all subspecies of the gray wolf (<i>Canis lupus</i>) that are not <span class="Latn" lang="en">dingoes</span> or <span class="Latn" lang="en">dogs</span>.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">Check out my pet. He's a <b>wolf</b>.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>A man who makes amorous advances to many women.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">music</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A wolf tone or wolf note.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The soft violin solo was marred by persistent <b>wolves</b>.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">figuratively</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Any very ravenous, rapacious, or destructive person or thing; especially, want; starvation.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1918</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W._B._Maxwell" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:W. B. Maxwell">W. B. Maxwell</a>,  chapter 7, in  <cite><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://openlibrary.org/works/OL1097634W">The Mirror and the Lamp</a></cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">“<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> Churchill, my dear fellow, we have such greedy sharks, and <b>wolves</b> in lamb's clothing. Oh, dear, there's so much to tell you, so many warnings to give you, but all that must be postponed for the moment.”</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">They toiled hard to keep the <b>wolf</b> from the door.</i></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">the bee wolf</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>One of the destructive, and usually hairy, larvae of several species of beetles and grain moths.</li>
<li>A white worm, or maggot, which infests granaries.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> An eating ulcer or sore. See <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">lupus</i>.
<ul><li><span class="maintenance-line" style="color: 777777;">(Can we date this quote by Jeremy Taylor and provide title, author's full name, and other details?)</span>
<dl><dd>If God should send a cancer upon thy face, or a <b>wolf</b> into thy side</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>A willying machine.
<dl><dd><span class="maintenance-line" style="color: 777777;">(Can we find and add a quotation of Knight to this entry?)</span></dd></dl></li></ol>
<div style="background-color: f0f0f0;">
<p><i>Part or all of this entry has been imported from the 1913 edition of </i>Webster’s Dictionary<i>, which is now free of copyright and hence in the public domain. The imported definitions may be significantly out of date, and any more recent senses may be completely missing.<br />(See the entry for <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.websters1913.com/words/Wolf">wolf</a> in </i>Webster’s Revised Unabridged Dictionary<i>, G. amp; C. Merriam, 1913.)</i>
</p>
</div>

<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">wolf</strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">wolfs</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">wolfing</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">wolfed</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To devour; to gobble; to eat (something) voraciously.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1987</b>,  James Ellroy,  <cite>The Black Dahlia</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">After a <b>wolfed</b> burger dinner, I called the night number at Administrative Vice and inquired about known lesbian gathering places.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2013</b>,  Neil Martin,  <cite>Collected Stories of the Sea</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Vicars seated himself and began <b>wolfing</b> a sandwich.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> slang</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To make amorous advances to many women; to hit on women; to cruise for sex.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1949</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nelson_Algren" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Nelson Algren">Nelson Algren</a>,  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Man_with_the_Golden_Arm_(novel)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Man with the Golden Arm (novel)">The Man with the Golden Arm</a></cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">[1940s Chicago punk:] ‘I’ve seen a thing or two in my time,’ he still liked to boast, ‘that was how I found out the best place for <b>wolfin’</b> ain’t the taverns. It ain’t in dance halls ’r on North Clark on Saturday night. It’s in the front row in Sunday school on Sunday mornin’. Oh yeh, I know a thing or two, I been around.’</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To hunt for wolves.</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> won (13816)</h1><br><hr><hr><h3><span id=".D0.9C.D0.BE.D1.80.D1.84.D0.BE.D0.BB.D0.BE.D0.B3.D0.B8.D1.87.D0.B5.D1.81.D0.BA.D0.B8.D0.B5_.D0.B8_.D1.81.D0.B8.D0.BD.D1.82.D0.B0.D0.BA.D1.81.D0.B8.D1.87.D0.B5.D1.81.D0.BA.D0.B8.D0.B5_.D1.81.D0.B2.D0.BE.D0.B9.D1.81.D1.82.D0.B2.D0.B0"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Морфологические_и_синтаксические_свойства"></span></h3>

<p><b>win</b>
</p><p><a href = vnd.unilang:существительное.html>Существи́тельное</a>.
</p>
